## Answer: No C++ Files Implement Both v2 and v3 xDS Handling

**The definitive finding across all four repositories is: no C++ source file implements simultaneous v2 + v3 xDS API handling.** All four repos represent a post-migration, v3-only state.

### What was examined and why it doesn't qualify

#### `envoy--v1.31.2` — 19 C++ files documented, all v3-only

| File | Why it doesn't qualify |

We build a reverse map from resource type URL to\n  // service methods (versioned by transport_api_version). We explicitly enumerate all services,\n  // since DescriptorPool doesn't support iterating over all descriptors, due its lazy load design,\n  // see https://www.mail-archive.com/protobuf@googlegroups.com/msg04540.html.\n  for (absl::string_view name : {\n           \"envoy.service.route.v3.RouteDiscoveryService\",\n           \"envoy.service.route.v3.ScopedRoutesDiscoveryService\",\n           \"envoy.service.route.v3.ScopedRoutesDiscoveryService\",\n           \"envoy.service.route.v3.VirtualHostDiscoveryService\",\n           \"envoy.service.secret.v3.SecretDiscoveryService\",\n           \"envoy.service.cluster.v3.ClusterDiscoveryService\",\n           \"envoy.service.endpoint.v3.EndpointDiscoveryService\",\n           \"envoy.service.endpoint.v3.LocalityEndpointDiscoveryService\",\n           \"envoy.service.listener.v3.ListenerDiscoveryService\",\n           \"envoy.service.runtime.v3.RuntimeDiscoveryService\",\n           \"envoy.service.extension.v3.ExtensionConfigDiscoveryService\",\n       }) {\n    const TypeUrl resource_type_url = getResourceTypeUrl(name);\n    V3Service& service = (*type_url_to_versioned_service_map)[resource_type_url];\n\n    const auto* service_desc =\n        Protobuf::DescriptorPool::generated_pool()->FindServiceByName(std::string(name));\n    ASSERT(service_desc != nullptr, fmt::format(\"{} missing\", name));\n    ASSERT(service_desc->options().HasExtension(envoy::annotations::resource));\n\n    // We populate the service methods that are known below, but it's possible that some\n    // services don't implement all, e.g. VHDS doesn't support SotW or REST.\n    for (int method_index = 0; "#include \"source/common/config/type_to_endpoint.h\"\n\n#include \"envoy/annotations/resource.pb.h\"\n\n#include \"source/common/grpc/common.h\"\n\n// API_NO_BOOST_FILE\n\nnamespace Envoy {\nnamespace Config {\n\nnamespace {\n\n// A service's name, e.g. \"envoy.api.v2.RouteDiscoveryService\",\n// \"envoy.service.route.v3.RouteDiscoveryService\".\nusing ServiceName = std::string;\n\n// A resource type URL. For example: \"type.googleapis.com/envoy.api.v2.RouteConfiguration\".\nusing TypeUrl = std::string;\n\nTypeUrl getResourceTypeUrl(absl::string_view service_name) {\n  const auto* service_desc = Protobuf::DescriptorPool::generated_pool()->FindServiceByName(\n      static_cast<ServiceName>(service_name));\n  ASSERT(service_desc != nullptr, fmt::format(\"{} missing\", service_name));\n  ASSERT(service_desc->options().HasExtension(envoy::annotations::resource));\n\n  return Grpc::Common::typeUrl(\n      service_desc->options().GetExtension(envoy::annotations::resource).type());\n}\n\n// A method name, e.g. \"envoy.api.v2.RouteDiscoveryService.StreamRoutes\".\nusing MethodName = std::string;\n\n// This holds  discovery types.\nstruct V3Service {\n  MethodName sotw_grpc_;\n  MethodName delta_grpc_;\n  MethodName rest_;\n};\n\nusing TypeUrlToV3ServiceMap = absl::flat_hash_map<TypeUrl, V3Service>;\n\nTypeUrlToV3ServiceMap* buildTypeUrlToServiceMap() {\n  auto* type_url_to_versioned_service_map = new TypeUrlToV3ServiceMap();\n\n  // This happens once in the lifetime of Envoy. We build a reverse map from resource type URL to\n  // service methods (versioned by transport_api_version). We explicitly enumerate all services,\n  // since DescriptorPool doesn't support iterating over all descriptors, due its lazy load design,\n  // see https://www.mail-archive.com/protobuf@googlegroups.com/msg04540.html.\n  for (absl::string_view name : {\n           \"envoy.service.route.v3.RouteDiscoveryService\",\n           \"envoy.service.route.v3.ScopedRoutesDiscoveryService\",\n           \"envoy.service.route.v3.ScopedRoutesDiscoveryService\",\n           \"envoy.service.route.v3.VirtualHostDiscoveryService\",\n           \"envoy.service.secret.v3.SecretDiscoveryService\",\n           \"envoy.service.cluster.v3.ClusterDiscoveryService\",\n           \"envoy.service.endpoint.v3.EndpointDiscoveryService\",\n           \"envoy.service.endpoint.v3.LocalityEndpointDiscoveryService\",\n           \"envoy.service.listener.v3.ListenerDiscoveryService\",\n           \"envoy.service.runtime.v3.RuntimeDiscoveryService\",\n           \"envoy.service.extension.v3.ExtensionConfigDiscoveryService\",\n       }) {\n    const TypeUrl resource_type_url = getResourceTypeUrl(name);\n    V3Service& service = (*type_url_to_versioned_service_map)[resource_type_url];\n\n    const auto* service_desc =\n        Protobuf::DescriptorPool::generated_pool()->FindServiceByName(std::string(name));\n    ASSERT(service_desc != nullptr, fmt::format(\"{} missing\", name));\n    ASSERT(service_desc->options().HasExtension(envoy::annotations::resource));\n\n    // We populate the service methods that are known below, but it's possible that some\n    // services don't implement all, e.g. VHDS doesn't support SotW or REST.\n    for (int method_index = 0; method_index < service_desc->method_count(); ++method_index) {\n      const auto& method_desc = *service_desc->method(method_index);\n      if (absl::StartsWith(method_desc.name(), \"Stream\")) {\n        service.sotw_grpc_ = method_desc.full_name();\n      } else if (absl::StartsWith(method_desc.name(), \"Delta\")) {\n        service.delta_grpc_ = method_desc.full_name();\n      } else if (absl::StartsWith(method_desc.name(), \"Fetch\")) {\n        service.rest_ = method_desc.full_name();\n      } else {\n        ASSERT(false, \"Unknown xDS service method\");\n      }\n    }\n  }\n  return type_url_to_versioned_service_map;\n}\n\nTypeUrlToV3ServiceMap& typeUrlToV3ServiceMap() {\n  static TypeUrlToV3ServiceMap* type_url_to_versioned_service_map = buildTypeUrlToServiceMap();\n  return *type_url_to_versioned_service_map;\n}\n\n} // namespace\n\nconst Protobuf::MethodDescriptor& deltaGrpcMethod(absl::string_view type_url) {\n  const auto it = typeUrlToV3ServiceMap().find(static_cast<TypeUrl>(type_url));\n  ASSERT(it != typeUrlToV3ServiceMap().cend());\n  return *Protobuf::DescriptorPool::generated_pool()->FindMethodByName(it->second.delta_grpc_);\n}\n\nconst Protobuf::MethodDescriptor& sotwGrpcMethod(absl::string_view type_url) {\n  const auto it = typeUrlToV3ServiceMap().find(static_cast<TypeUrl>(type_url));\n  ASSERT(it != typeUrlToV3ServiceMap().cend());\n  return *Protobuf::DescriptorPool::generated_pool()->FindMethodByName(it->second.sotw_grpc_);\n}\n\nconst Protobuf::MethodDescriptor& restMethod(absl::string_view type_url) {\n  const auto it = typeUrlToV3ServiceMap().find(static_cast<TypeUrl>(type_url));\n  ASSERT(it != typeUrlToV3ServiceMap().cend());\n  return *Protobuf::DescriptorPool::generated_pool()->FindMethodByName(it->second.rest_);\n}\n\n} // namespace Config\n} // namespace Envoy"

Several xDS callers might ask for a subscription to the same\n// resource name \"X\". The xDS machinery must return to each their very own subscription to X.\n// The xDS machinery's \"watch\" concept accomplishes that, while avoiding parallel redundant xDS\n// requests for X. Each of those subscriptions is viewed as a \"watch\" on X, while behind the scenes\n// there is just a single real subscription to that resource name.\n//\n// This class maintains the watches<-->subscription mapping: it\n// 1) delivers updates to all interested watches, and\n// 2) tracks which resource names should be {added to,removed from} the subscription when the\n//    {first,last} watch on a resource name is {added,removed}.\n//\n// #1 is accomplished by WatchMap's implementation of the SubscriptionCallbacks interface.\n// This interface allows the xDS client to just throw each xDS update message it receives directly\n// into WatchMap::onConfigUpdate, rather than having to track the various watches' callbacks.\n//\n// The information for #2 is returned by updateWatchInterest(); the caller should use it to\n// update the subscription accordingly.\n//\n// A WatchMap is assumed to be dedicated to a single type_url type of resource (EDS, CDS, etc).\n//\n// The WatchMap can also store the fetched resources in a cache, and allow others to fetch\n// resources directly from the cache. This is done for EDS in the following case:\n// Assume an active EDS cluster exists with some load-assignment that is kept in the cache.\n// If the cluster is updated, and no load-assignment is sent from the xDS server, the\n// cached version will be used.\n// The WatchMap is responsible to update the cache with the resource contents, and it is\n// up to the specific xDS type subscription handler (i.e., EdsClusterImpl), to fetch\n// the resource from the cache.\nclass WatchMap : public UntypedConfigUpdateCallbacks, public Logger::Loggable<Logger::Id::config> {\npublic:\n  WatchMap(const bool use_namespace_matching, const std::string& type_url,\n           CustomConfigValidators& config_validators, EdsResourcesCacheOptRef eds_resources_cache)\n      : use_namespace_matching_(use_namespace_matching), type_url_(type_url),\n        config_validators_(config_validators), eds_resources_cache_(eds_resources_cache) {\n    // If eds resources cache is provided, then the type must be ClusterLoadAssignment.\n    ASSERT(!eds_resources_cache_.has_value() ||\n           (type_url == Config::getTypeUrl<envoy::config::endpoint::v3::ClusterLoadAssignment>()));\n  }\n\n  // Adds 'callbacks' to the WatchMap, with every possible resource being watched.\n  // (Use updateWatchInterest() to narrow it down to some specific names).\n  // Returns the newly added watch, to be used with updateWatchInterest and removeWatch.\n  Watch* addWatch(SubscriptionCallbacks& callbacks, OpaqueResourceDecoder& resource_decoder);\n\n  // Updates the set of resource names that the given watch should watch.\n  // Returns any resource name additions/removals that are unique across all watches. That is:\n  // 1) if 'resources' contains X and no other watch cares about X, X will be in added_.\n  // 2) if 'resources' does not contain Y, and this watch was the only one that cared about Y,\n  //    Y will be in removed_.\n  AddedRemoved updateWatchInterest(Watch* watch,\n                                   const absl::flat_hash_set<std::string>& update_to_these_names);\n\n  // Expects that the watch to be removed has already had all of its resource names removed via\n  // updateWatchInterest().\n  void removeWatch(Watch* watch);\n\n  // UntypedConfigUpdateCallbacks.\n  void onConfigUpdate(const Protobuf::RepeatedPtrField<ProtobufWkt::Any>& resources,\n                      const std::string& version_info) override;\n\n  void onConfigUpdate(const std::vector<DecodedResourcePtr>& resources,\n                      const std::string& version_info) override;\n\n  void onConfigUpdate(\n      const Protobuf::RepeatedPtrField<envoy::service::discovery::v3::Resource>& added_resources,\n      const Protobuf::RepeatedPtrField<std::string>& removed_resources,\n      const std::string& system_version_info) override;\n  void onConfigUpdateFailed(ConfigUpdateFailureReason reason, const EnvoyException* e) override;\n\n  WatchMap(const WatchMap&) = delete;\n  WatchMap& operator=(const WatchMap&) = delete;\n\nprivate:\n  void removeDeferredWatches();\n\n  // Given a list of names that are new to an individual watch, returns those names that are in fact\n  // new to the entire subscription.\n  absl::flat_hash_set<std::string>\n  findAdditions(const absl::flat_hash_set<std::string>& newly_added_to_watch, Watch* watch);\n\n  // Given a list of names that an individual watch no longer cares about, returns those names that\n  // in fact the entire subscription no longer cares about.\n  absl::flat_hash_set<std::string>\n  findRemovals(const absl::flat_hash_set<std::string>& newly_removed_from_watch, Watch* watch);\n\n  // Returns the union of watch_interest_[resource_name] and wildcard_watches_.\n  absl::flat_hash_set<Watch*> watchesInterestedIn(const std::string& resource_name);\n\n  absl::flat_hash_set<std::unique_ptr<Watch>> watches_;\n\n  // Watches whose interest set is currently empty, which is interpreted as \"everything\".\n  absl::flat_hash_set<Watch*> wildcard_watches_;\n\n  // Watches that have been removed inside the call stack of the WatchMap's onConfigUpdate(). This\n  // can happen when a watch's onConfigUpdate() results in another watch being removed via\n  // removeWatch().\n  std::unique_ptr<absl::flat_hash_set<Watch*>> deferred_removed_during_update_;\n\n  // Maps a resource name to the set of watches interested in that resource. Has two purposes:\n  // 1) Acts as a reference count; no watches care anymore ==> the resource can be removed.\n  // 2) Enables efficient lookup of all interested watches when a resource has been updated.\n  absl::flat_hash_map<std::string, absl::flat_hash_set<Watch*>> watch_interest_;\n\n  const bool use_namespace_matching_;\n  const std::string type_url_;\n  CustomConfigValidators& config_validators_;\n  EdsResourcesCacheOptRef eds_resources_cache_;\n};\n\n} // namespace Config\n} // namespace Envoy"

"#pragma once\n\n#include \"source/common/common/logger.h\"\n#include \"source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/grpc_stream.h\"\n\nnamespace Envoy {\nnamespace Config {\n\n/**\n * This class arbitrates between two config providers of the same GrpcMux -\n * the primary and the failover. Envoy always prefers fetching config from the\n * primary source, but if not available, it will fetch the config from the failover\n * source until the primary is again available.\n *\n * This class owns the state for the GrpcMux primary and failover streams, and\n * proxies the gRPC-stream functionality to either the primary or the failover config sources.\n * The failover source is optional and will only be used if given in the c'tor.\n *\n * Failover is supported in both\n * SotW (RequestType = envoy::service::discovery::v3::DiscoveryRequest,\n *   ResponseType = envoy::service::discovery::v3::DiscoveryResponse), and\n * Delta-xDS (RequestType = envoy::service::discovery::v3::DeltaDiscoveryRequest,\n *   ResponseType = envoy::service::discovery::v3::DeltaDiscoveryResponse).\n * Both the primary and failover streams are either SotW or Delta-xDS.\n *\n * The use of this class will be as follows: the GrpcMux object will own an instance of\n * the GrpcMuxFailover. The GrpcMuxFailover will own 2 GrpcStreams, primary and failover.\n * Each of the primary and secondary streams will invoke GrpcStreamCallbacks\n * on their corresponding objects (also owned by the GrpcMuxFailover). These invocations\n * will be followed by the GrpcMuxFailover calling the GrpcStreamCallbacks on the GrpcMux\n * object that initialized it.\n *\n * Note: this class is WIP and should be considered alpha!\n * At the moment, the supported policy is as follows:\n * The GrpcMuxFailover attempts to establish a connection to the primary source. Once a response is\n * received from the primary source it will be considered available, and the failover will not be\n * used. Any future reconnection attempts will be to the primary source only.\n * However, if no response is received from the primary source, and accessing the primary has\n * failed 2 times in a row, the GrpcMuxFailover will attempt to establish a connection to the\n * failover source. If a response from the failover source is received, only the failover source\n * will be used.\n * If the failover source is unavailable, the GrpcMuxFailover will alternate between attempts\n * to reconnect to the primary source and the failover source.\n * In the future, this behavior may change, and the GrpcMuxFailover will always\n * prefer the primary source, even if prior connection to the failover was successful.\n * TODO(adisuissa): The number of consecutive failures is currently statically\n * defined, and may be converted to a config field in the future.\n */\ntemplate <class RequestType, class ResponseType>\nclass GrpcMuxFailover : public GrpcStreamInterface<RequestType, ResponseType>,\n                        public Logger::Loggable<Logger::Id::config> {\npublic:\n  static constexpr uint32_t DefaultFailoverBackoffMilliseconds = 500;\n\n  // A GrpcStream creator function that receives the stream callbacks and returns a\n  // GrpcStream object. This is introduced to facilitate dependency injection for\n  // testing and will be used to create the primary and failover streams.\n  using GrpcStreamCreator = std::function<GrpcStreamInterfacePtr<RequestType, ResponseType>(\n      GrpcStreamCallbacks<ResponseType>* stream_callbacks)>;\n\n  GrpcMuxFailover(GrpcStreamCreator primary_stream_creator,\n                  absl::optional<GrpcStreamCreator> failover_stream_creator,\n                  GrpcStreamCallbacks<ResponseType>& grpc_mux_callbacks,\n                  Event::Dispatcher& dispatcher)\n      : grpc_mux_callbacks_(grpc_mux_callbacks), primary_callbacks_(*this),\n        primary_grpc_stream_(std::move(primary_stream_creator(&primary_callbacks_))),\n        connecting_to_primary_(false), connecting_to_failover_(false),\n        connected_to_(ConnectedState::None), ever_connected_to_(ConnectedState::None) {\n    ASSERT(primary_grpc_stream_ != nullptr);\n    if (failover_stream_creator.has_value()) {\n      ENVOY_LOG(warn, \"Using xDS-Failover. "package sotw\n\nimport (\n        \"google.golang.org/grpc/codes\"\n        \"google.golang.org/grpc/status\"\n\n        discovery \"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/service/discovery/v3\"\n        \"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/pkg/cache/types\"\n        \"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/pkg/cache/v3\"\n        \"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/pkg/server/stream/v3\"\n)\n\n// process handles a bi-di stream request\nfunc (s *server) processADS(sw *streamWrapper, reqCh chan *discovery.DiscoveryRequest) error {\n        // Create a buffered multiplexed channel the size of the known resource types.\n        respChan := make(chan cache.Response, types.UnknownType)\n\n        // Instead of creating a separate channel for each incoming request and abandoning the old one\n        // This algorithm uses (and reuses) a single channel for all request types and guarantees\n        // the server will send updates over the wire in an ordered fashion.\n        // Downside is there is no longer back pressure per resource.\n        // There is potential for a dropped response from the cache but this is not impactful\n        // to the client since SOTW version handling is global and a new sequence will be\n        // initiated on a new request.\n        processAllExcept := func(typeURL string) error {\n                for {\n                        select {\n                        // We watch the multiplexed ADS channel for incoming responses.\n                        case res := <-respChan:\n                                if res.GetRequest().GetTypeUrl() != typeURL {\n                                        if err := sw.send(res); err != nil {\n                                                return err\n                                        }\n                                }\n                        default:\n                                return nil\n                        }\n                }\n        }\n\n        // This control loop strictly orders resources when running in ADS mode.\n        // It should be treated as a child process of the original process() loop\n        // and should return on close of stream or error. This will cause the\n        // cleanup routines in the parent process() loop to execute.\n        for {\n                select {\n                case <-s.ctx.Done():\n                        return nil\n                // We only watch the multiplexed channel since we don't use per watch channels.\n                case res := <-respChan:\n                        if err := sw.send(res); err != nil {\n                                return status.Errorf(codes.Unavailable, err.Error())\n                        }\n                case req, ok := <-reqCh:\n                        // Input stream ended or failed.\n                        if !ok {\n                                return nil\n                        }\n\n                        // Received an empty request over the request channel. Can't respond.\n                        if req == nil {\n                                return status.Errorf(codes.Unavailable, \"empty request\")\n                        }\n\n                        // Only first request is guaranteed to hold node info so if it's missing, reassign.\n                        if req.GetNode() != nil {\n                                sw.node = req.GetNode()\n                        } else {\n                                req.Node = sw.node\n                        }\n\n                        // type URL is required for ADS but is implicit for xDS\n                        typeURL := req.GetTypeUrl()\n                        if typeURL == \"\" {\n                                return status.Errorf(codes.InvalidArgument, \"type URL is required for ADS\")\n                        }\n\n                        if s.callbacks != nil {\n                                if err := s.callbacks.OnStreamRequest(sw.ID, req); err != nil {\n                                        return err\n                                }\n                        }\n\n                        var subscription stream.Subscription\n                        w, ok := sw.watches.responders[typeURL]\n                        if ok {\n                                if w.nonce != \"\" && req.GetResponseNonce() != w.nonce {\n                                        // The request does not match the stream nonce, ignore it as per\n                                        // https://www.envoyproxy.io/docs/envoy/v1.28.0/api-docs/xds_protocol#resource-updates\n                                        // Ignore this request and wait for the next one\n                                        // This behavior is being discussed in https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/10363\n                                        // as it might create a race in edge cases, but it matches the current protocol definition\n                                        s.opts.Logger.Infof(\"[sotw ads] Skipping request as nonce is stale for %s\", typeURL)\n                                        break\n                                }\n\n                                // We found an existing watch\n                                // Close it to ensure the Cache will not reply to it while we modify the subscription state\n                                w.close()\n\n                                // Only process if we have an existing watch otherwise go ahead and create.\n                                if err := processAllExcept(typeURL); err != nil {\n                                        return err\n                                }\n\n                                subscription = w.sub\n                                subscription.SetResourceSubscription(req.GetResourceNames())\n                        } else {\n                                s.opts.Logger.Debugf(\"[sotw ads] New subscription for type %s and stream %d\", typeURL, sw.ID)\n                                subscription = stream.NewSotwSubscription(req.GetResourceNames(), s.opts.IsLegacyWildcardActive(typeURL))\n                        }\n\n                        cancel, err := s.cache.CreateWatch(req, subscription, respChan)\n                        if err != nil {\n                                return err\n                        }\n                        sw.watches.addWatch(typeURL, &watch{\n                                cancel:   cancel,\n                                response: respChan,\n                                sub:      subscription,\n                        })\n                }\n        }\n}"

"package stream\n\nconst (\n        explicitWildcard = \"*\"\n)\n\n// Subscription stores the server view of a given type subscription in a stream.\ntype Subscription struct {\n        // wildcard indicates if the subscription currently has a wildcard watch.\n        wildcard bool\n\n        // allowLegacyWildcard indicates that the stream never provided any resource\n        // and is de facto wildcard.\n        // As soon as a resource or an explicit subscription to wildcard is provided,\n        // this flag will be set to false\n        allowLegacyWildcard bool\n\n        // subscribedResourceNames provides the resources explicitly requested by the client\n        // This list might be non-empty even when set as wildcard.\n        subscribedResourceNames map[string]struct{}\n\n        // returnedResources contains the resources acknowledged by the client and the acknowledged versions.\n        returnedResources map[string]string\n}\n\n// newSubscription initializes a subscription state.\nfunc newSubscription(emptyRequest, allowLegacyWildcard bool, initialResourceVersions map[string]string) Subscription {\n        // By default we set the subscription as a wildcard only if the request was empty\n        // and in legacy mode. Later on, outside of this constructor, when we actually\n        // process the request, if the request was non-empty, it may have an\n        // explicit wildcard subscription, in which case\n        // we will set the wildcard field on the subscription accordingly.\n        wildcard := emptyRequest && allowLegacyWildcard\n\n        state := Subscription{\n                wildcard:                wildcard,\n                allowLegacyWildcard:     allowLegacyWildcard,\n                subscribedResourceNames: map[string]struct{}{},\n                returnedResources:       initialResourceVersions,\n        }\n\n        if initialResourceVersions == nil {\n                state.returnedResources = make(map[string]string)\n        }\n\n        return state\n}\n\nfunc NewSotwSubscription(subscribed []string, allowLegacyWildcard bool) Subscription {\n        sub := newSubscription(len(subscribed) == 0, allowLegacyWildcard, nil)\n        sub.SetResourceSubscription(subscribed)\n        return sub\n}\n\n// SetResourceSubscription updates the subscribed resources (including the wildcard state)\n// based on the full state of subscribed resources provided in the request\n// Used in sotw subscriptions\n// Behavior is based on\n// https://www.envoyproxy.io/docs/envoy/latest/api-docs/xds_protocol#how-the-client-specifies-what-resources-to-return\nfunc (s *Subscription) SetResourceSubscription(subscribed []string) {\n        if s.allowLegacyWildcard {\n                if len(subscribed) == 0 {\n                        // We were wildcard based on legacy behavior and still don't request any resource\n                        // The watch remains wildcard\n                        return\n                }\n\n                // A resource was provided (might be an explicit wildcard)\n                // Documentation states that we should no longer allow to fallback to the previous case\n                // and no longer setting wildcard would no longer subscribe to anything\n                s.allowLegacyWildcard = false\n        }\n\n        subscribedResources := make(map[string]struct{}, len(subscribed))\n        explicitWildcardSet := false\n        for _, resource := range subscribed {\n                if resource == explicitWildcard {\n                        explicitWildcardSet = true\n                } else {\n                        subscribedResources[resource] = struct{}{}\n                }\n        }\n\n        if !explicitWildcardSet {\n                // Cleanup resources no longer subscribed to.\n                // This ensures later subscriptions will trigger responses,\n                // even if the version has not changed\n                for resource := range s.returnedResources {\n                        if _, ok := subscribedResources[resource]; !ok {\n                                delete(s.returnedResources, resource)\n                        }\n                }\n        }\n\n        // Explicit subscription to wildcard as we are not in legacy wildcard behavior\n        s.wildcard = explicitWildcardSet\n        s.subscribedResourceNames = subscribedResources\n}\n\nfunc NewDeltaSubscription(subscribed, unsubscribed []string, initialResourceVersions map[string]string, allowLegacyWildcard bool) Subscription {\n        sub := newSubscription(len(subscribed) == 0, allowLegacyWildcard, initialResourceVersions)\n        sub.UpdateResourceSubscriptions(subscribed, unsubscribed)\n        return sub\n}\n\n// UpdateResourceSubscriptions updates the subscribed resources (including the wildcard state)\n// based on newly subscribed or unsubscribed resources\n// Used in delta subscriptions\nfunc (s *Subscription) UpdateResourceSubscriptions(subscribed, unsubscribed []string) {\n        // Handles legacy wildcard behavior first to exit if we are still in this behavior\n        if s.allowLegacyWildcard {\n                // The protocol (as of v1.36.0) only references subscribed as triggering\n                // exiting legacy wildcard behavior, so we currently not check unsubscribed\n                if len(subscribed) == 0 {\n                        // We were wildcard based on legacy behavior and still don't request any resource\n                        // The watch remains wildcard\n                        return\n                }\n\n                // A resource was provided (might be an explicit wildcard)\n                // Documentation states that we should no longer allow to fallback to the previous case\n                // and no longer setting wildcard would no longer subscribe to anything\n                // The watch does resource == explicitWildcard {\n                        s.wildcard = false\n                        continue\n                }\n                if _, ok := s.subscribedResourceNames[resource]; ok && s.wildcard {\n                        // The XDS protocol states that:\n                        // * if a watch is currently wildcard\n                        // * a resource is explicitly unsubscribed by name\n                        // Then the control-plane must return in the response whether the resource is removed (if no longer present for this node)\n                        // or still existing. In the latter case the entire resource must be returned, same as if it had been created or updated\n                        // To achieve that, we mark the resource as having been returned with an empty version. While creating the response, the cache will either:\n                        // * detect the version change, and return the resource (as an update)\n                        // * detect the resource deletion, and set it as removed in the response\n                        s.returnedResources[resource] = \"\"\n                } else {\n                        // Cleanup unsubscribed resources. This avoids returning a response\n                        // if the versions have not changed\n                        delete(s.returnedResources, resource)\n                }\n                delete(s.subscribedResourceNames, resource)\n        }\n}\n\n// SubscribedResources returns the list of resources currently explicitly subscribed to\n// If the request is set to wildcard it may be empty\nfunc (s Subscription) SubscribedResources() map[string]struct{} {\n        return s.subscribedResourceNames\n}\n\n// IsWildcard returns whether or not the subscription currently has a wildcard watch\nfunc (s Subscription) IsWildcard() bool {\n        return s.wildcard\n}\n\n// ReturnedResources returns the list of resources returned to the client\n// and their version\nfunc (s Subscription) ReturnedResources() map[string]string {\n        return s.returnedResources\n}\n\n// SetReturnedResources sets a list of resource versions currently known by the client\n// The cache can use this state to compute resources added/updated/deleted\nfunc (s *Subscription) SetReturnedResources(resourceVersions map[string]string) {\n        s.returnedResources = resourceVersions\n}"

"# API versioning guidelines\n\nThe Envoy project and [xDS working group](https://github.com/cncf/xds) take API stability and\nversioning seriously. Providing stable APIs is a necessary step in ensuring API adoption and success\nof the ecosystem. Below we articulate the API versioning guidelines that aim to deliver this\nstability.\n\n# API semantic versioning\n\nThe Envoy APIs consist of a family of packages, e.g. `envoy.admin.v3alpha`,\n`envoy.service.trace.v3`. Each package is independently versioned with a protobuf semantic\nversioning scheme based on https://cloud.google.com/apis/design/versioning.\n\nThe major version for a package is captured in its name (and directory structure). E.g. version 3\nof the tracing API package is named `envoy.service.trace.v3` and its constituent protos are located\nin `api/envoy/service/trace/v3`. Every protobuf must live directly in a versioned package namespace,\nwe do not allow subpackages such as `envoy.service.trace.v3.somethingelse`.\n\nIn everyday discussion and GitHub labels, we refer to the `v2`, `v3`, `vN`, `...` APIs. This has a\nspecific technical meaning. Any given message in the Envoy API, e.g. the `Bootstrap` at\n`envoy.config.bootstrap.v3.Bootstrap`, will transitively reference a number of packages in the Envoy\nAPI. These may be at `vN`, `v(N-1)`, etc. The Envoy API is technically a DAG of versioned package\nnamespaces. When we talk about the `vN xDS API`, we really refer to the `N` of the root\nconfiguration resources (e.g. bootstrap, xDS resources such as `Cluster`). The\nv3 API bootstrap configuration is `envoy.config.bootstrap.v3.Bootstrap`.\n\n# Backwards compatibility\n\nIn general, within a package's major API version, we do not allow any breaking changes. The guiding\nprinciple is that neither the wire format nor protobuf compiler generated language bindings should\nexperience a backward compatible break on a change. Specifically:\n\n* Fields should not be renumbered or have their types changed. This is standard proto development\n  procedure.\n\n* Renaming of fields or package namespaces for a proto must not occur. This is inherently dangerous,\n  since:\n  * Field renames break wire compatibility. This is stricter than standard proto development\n    procedure in the sense that it does not break binary wire format. However, it **does** break\n    loading of YAML/JSON into protos as well as text protos. Since we consider YAML/JSON to be first\n    class inputs, we must not change field names.\n\n  * For service definitions, the gRPC endpoint URL is inferred from package namespace, so this will\n    break client/server communication.\n\n  * For a message embedded in an `Any` object, the type URL, which the package namespace is a part\n    of, may be used by Envoy or other API consuming code. Currently, this applies to the top-level\n    resources embedded in `DiscoveryResponse` objects, e.g. `Cluster`, `Listener`, etc.\n\n  * Consuming code will break and require source code changes to match the API changes.\n\n* Some other changes are considered breaking for Envoy APIs that are usually considered safe in\n  terms of protobuf wire compatibility:\n  * Upgrading a singleton field to a repeated, e.g. `uint32 foo = 1;` to `repeated uint32 foo = 1`.\n    This changes the JSON wire representation and hence is considered a breaking change.\n\n  * Wrapping an existing field with `oneof`. This has no protobuf or JSON/YAML wire implications,\n    but is disruptive to various consuming stubs in languages such as Go, creating unnecessary\n    churn."

For example: \"type.googleapis.com/envoy.api.v2.RouteConfiguration\".\nusing TypeUrl = std::string;\n\nTypeUrl getResourceTypeUrl(absl::string_view service_name) {\n  const auto* service_desc = Protobuf::DescriptorPool::generated_pool()->FindServiceByName(\n      static_cast<ServiceName>(service_name));\n  ASSERT(service_desc != nullptr, fmt::format(\"{} missing\", service_name));\n  ASSERT(service_desc->options().HasExtension(envoy::annotations::resource));\n\n  return Grpc::Common::typeUrl(\n      service_desc->options().GetExtension(envoy::annotations::resource).type());\n}\n\n// A method name, e.g. \"envoy.api.v2.RouteDiscoveryService.StreamRoutes\".\nusing MethodName = std::string;\n\n// This holds  discovery types.\nstruct V3Service {\n  MethodName sotw_grpc_;\n  MethodName delta_grpc_;\n  MethodName rest_;\n};\n\nusing TypeUrlToV3ServiceMap = absl::flat_hash_map<TypeUrl, V3Service>;\n\nTypeUrlToV3ServiceMap* buildTypeUrlToServiceMap() {\n  auto* type_url_to_versioned_service_map = new TypeUrlToV3ServiceMap();\n\n  // This happens once in the lifetime of Envoy. We build a reverse map from resource type URL to\n  // service methods (versioned by transport_api_version). We explicitly enumerate all services,\n  // since DescriptorPool doesn't support iterating over all descriptors, due its lazy load design,\n  // see https://www.mail-archive.com/protobuf@googlegroups.com/msg04540.html.\n  for (absl::string_view name : {\n           \"envoy.service.route.v3.RouteDiscoveryService\",\n           \"envoy.service.route.v3.ScopedRoutesDiscoveryService\",\n           \"envoy.service.route.v3.ScopedRoutesDiscoveryService\",\n           \"envoy.service.route.v3.VirtualHostDiscoveryService\",\n           \"envoy.service.secret.v3.SecretDiscoveryService\",\n           \"envoy.service.cluster.v3.ClusterDiscoveryService\",\n           \"envoy.service.endpoint.v3.EndpointDiscoveryService\",\n           \"envoy.service.endpoint.v3.LocalityEndpointDiscoveryService\",\n           \"envoy.service.listener.v3.ListenerDiscoveryService\",\n           \"envoy.service.runtime.v3.RuntimeDiscoveryService\",\n           \"envoy.service.extension.v3.ExtensionConfigDiscoveryService\",\n       }) {\n    const TypeUrl resource_type_url = getResourceTypeUrl(name);\n    V3Service& service = (*type_url_to_versioned_service_map)[resource_type_url];\n\n    const auto* service_desc =\n        Protobuf::DescriptorPool::generated_pool()->FindServiceByName(std::string(name));\n    ASSERT(service_desc != nullptr, fmt::format(\"{} missing\", name));\n    ASSERT(service_desc->options().HasExtension(envoy::annotations::resource));\n\n    // We populate the service methods that are known below, but it's possible that some\n    // services don't implement all, e.g. VHDS doesn't support SotW or REST.\n    for (int method_index = 0; method_index < service_desc->method_count(); ++method_index) {\n      const auto& method_desc = *service_desc->method(method_index);\n      if (absl::StartsWith(method_desc.name(), \"Stream\")) {\n        service.sotw_grpc_ = method_desc.full_name();\n      } else if (absl::StartsWith(method_desc.name(), \"Delta\")) {\n        service.delta_grpc_ = method_desc.full_name();\n      } else if (absl::StartsWith(method_desc.name(), \"Fetch\")) {\n        service.rest_ = method_desc.full_name();\n      } else {\n        ASSERT(false, \"Unknown xDS service method\");\n      }\n    }\n  }\n  return type_url_to_versioned_service_map;\n}\n\nTypeUrlToV3ServiceMap& typeUrlToV3ServiceMap() {\n  static TypeUrlToV3ServiceMap* type_url_to_versioned_service_map = buildTypeUrlToServiceMap();\n  return *type_url_to_versioned_service_map;\n}\n\n} // namespace\n\nconst Protobuf::MethodDescriptor& deltaGrpcMethod(absl::string_view type_url) {\n  const auto it = typeUrlToV3ServiceMap().find(static_cast<TypeUrl>(type_url));\n  ASSERT(it != typeUrlToV3ServiceMap().cend());\n  return *Protobuf::DescriptorPool::generated_pool()->FindMethodByName(it->second.delta_grpc_);\n}\n\nconst Protobuf::MethodDescriptor& sotwGrpcMethod(absl::string_view type_url) {\n  const auto it = typeUrlToV3ServiceMap().find(static_cast<TypeUrl>(type_url));\n  ASSERT(it != typeUrlToV3ServiceMap().cend());\n  return *Protobuf::DescriptorPool::generated_pool()->FindMethodByName(it->second.sotw_grpc_);\n}\n\nconst Protobuf::MethodDescriptor& restMethod(absl::string_view type_url) {\n  const auto it = typeUrlToV3ServiceMap().find(static_cast<TypeUrl>(type_url));\n  ASSERT(it != typeUrlToV3ServiceMap().cend());\n  return *Protobuf::DescriptorPool::generated_pool()->FindMethodByName(it->second.rest_);\n}\n\n} // namespace Config\n} // namespace Envoy"

"#pragma once\n\n#include \"envoy/config/subscription.h\"\n#include \"envoy/config/xds_config_tracker.h\"\n#include \"envoy/event/dispatcher.h\"\n#include \"envoy/grpc/status.h\"\n#include \"envoy/local_info/local_info.h\"\n#include \"envoy/service/discovery/v3/discovery.pb.h\"\n\n#include \"source/common/common/assert.h\"\n#include \"source/common/common/logger.h\"\n#include \"source/common/config/api_version.h\"\n#include \"source/common/config/ttl.h\"\n#include \"source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/pausable_ack_queue.h\"\n#include \"source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/watch_map.h\"\n\n#include \"absl/container/node_hash_map.h\"\n\nnamespace Envoy {\nnamespace Config {\n\n// Tracks the xDS protocol state of an individual ongoing delta xDS session, i.e. a single type_url.\n// There can be multiple DeltaSubscriptionStates active. They will always all be blissfully\n// unaware of each other's existence, even when their messages are being multiplexed together by\n// ADS.\n//\n// There are two scenarios which affect how DeltaSubscriptionState manages the resources. First\n// scenario is when we are subscribed to a wildcard resource, and other scenario is when we are not.\n//\n// Delta subscription state also divides the resources it cached into three categories: requested,\n// wildcard and ambiguous.\n//\n// The \"requested\" category is for resources that we have explicitly asked for (either through the\n// initial set of resources or through the on-demand mechanism). Resources in this category are in\n// one of two states: \"complete\" and \"waiting for server\".\n//\n// \"Complete\" resources are resources about which the server sent us the information we need (for\n// now - just resource version).\n//\n// The \"waiting for server\" state is either for resources that we have just requested, but we still\n// didn't receive any version information from the server, or for the \"complete\" resources that,\n// according to the server, are gone, but we are still interested in them - in such case we strip\n// the information from the resource.\n//\n// The \"wildcard\" category is for resources that we are not explicitly interested in, but we are\n// indirectly interested through the subscription to the wildcard resource.\n//\n// The \"ambiguous\" category is for resources that we stopped being interested in, but we may still\n// be interested indirectly through the wildcard subscription. This situation happens because of the\n// xDS protocol limitation - the server isn't able to tell us that the resource we subscribed to is\n// also a part of our wildcard subscription. So when we unsubscribe from the resource, we need to\n// receive a confirmation from the server whether to keep the resource (which means that it was a\n// part of our wildcard subscription) or to drop it.\n//\n// Please refer to drawings (non-wildcard-resource-state-machine.png and\n// (wildcard-resource-state-machine.png) for visual depictions of the resource state machine.\n//\n// In the \"no wildcard subscription\" scenario all the cached resources should be in the \"requested\"\n// category. Resources are added to the category upon the explicit request and dropped when we\n// explicitly unsubscribe from it. Transitions between \"complete\" and \"waiting for server\" happen\n// when we receive messages from the server - if a resource in the message is in \"added resources\"\n// list (thus contains version information), the resource becomes \"complete\". If the resource in the\n// message is in \"removed resources\" list, it changes into the \"waiting for server\" state. If a\n// server sends us a resource that we didn't request, it's going to be ignored.\n//\n// In the \"wildcard subscription\" scenario, \"requested\" category is the same as in \"no wildcard\n// subscription\" scenario, with one exception - the unsubscribed \"complete\" resource is not removed\n// from the cache, but it's moved to the \"ambiguous\" resources instead. At this point we are waiting\n// for the server to tell us that this resource should be either moved to the \"wildcard\" resources,\n// or dropped. Resources in \"wildcard\" category are only added there or dropped from there by the\n// server. Resources from both \"wildcard\" and \"ambiguous\" categories can become \"requested\"\n// \"complete\" resources if we subscribe to them again.\n//\n// The delta subscription state transitions between the two scenarios depending on whether we are\n// subscribed to wildcard resource or not. Nothing special happens when we transition from \"no\n// wildcard subscription\" to \"wildcard subscription\" scenario, but when transitioning in the other\n// direction, we drop all the resources in \"wildcard\" and \"ambiguous\" categories.\nclass DeltaSubscriptionState : public Logger::Loggable<Logger::Id::config> {\npublic:\n  DeltaSubscriptionState(std::string type_url, UntypedConfigUpdateCallbacks& watch_map,"

"#pragma once\n\n#include \"source/common/common/logger.h\"\n#include \"source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/grpc_stream.h\"\n\nnamespace Envoy {\nnamespace Config {\n\n/**\n * This class arbitrates between two config providers of the same GrpcMux -\n * the primary and the failover. Envoy always prefers fetching config from the\n * primary source, but if not available, it will fetch the config from the failover\n * source until the primary is again available.\n *\n * This class owns the state for the GrpcMux primary and failover streams, and\n * proxies the gRPC-stream functionality to either the primary or the failover config sources.\n * The failover source is optional and will only be used if given in the c'tor.\n *\n * Failover is supported in both\n * SotW (RequestType = envoy::service::discovery::v3::DiscoveryRequest,\n *   ResponseType = envoy::service::discovery::v3::DiscoveryResponse), and\n * Delta-xDS (RequestType = envoy::service::discovery::v3::DeltaDiscoveryRequest,\n *   ResponseType = envoy::service::discovery::v3::DeltaDiscoveryResponse).\n * Both the primary and failover streams are either SotW or Delta-xDS.\n *\n * The use of this class will be as follows: the GrpcMux object will own an instance of\n * the GrpcMuxFailover. The GrpcMuxFailover will own 2 GrpcStreams, primary and failover.\n * Each of the primary and secondary streams will invoke GrpcStreamCallbacks\n * on their corresponding objects (also owned by the GrpcMuxFailover). These invocations\n * will be followed by the GrpcMuxFailover calling the GrpcStreamCallbacks on the GrpcMux\n * object that initialized it.\n *\n * Note: this class is WIP and should be considered alpha!\n * At the moment, the supported policy is as follows:\n * The GrpcMuxFailover attempts to establish a connection to the primary source. Once a response is\n * received from the primary source it will be considered available, and the failover will not be\n * used. Any future reconnection attempts will be to the primary source only.\n * However, if no response is received from the primary source, and accessing the primary has\n * failed 2 times in a row, the GrpcMuxFailover will attempt to establish a connection to the\n * failover source. If a response from the failover source is received, only the failover source\n * will be used.\n * If the failover source is unavailable, the GrpcMuxFailover will alternate between attempts\n * to reconnect to the primary source and the failover source.\n * In the future, this behavior may change, and the GrpcMuxFailover will always\n * prefer the primary source, even if prior connection to the failover was successful.\n * TODO(adisuissa): The number of consecutive failures is currently statically\n * defined, and may be converted to a config field in the future.\n */\ntemplate <class RequestType, class ResponseType>\nclass GrpcMuxFailover : public GrpcStreamInterface<RequestType, ResponseType>,\n                        public Logger::Loggable<Logger::Id::config> {\npublic:\n  static constexpr uint32_t DefaultFailoverBackoffMilliseconds = 500;\n\n  // A GrpcStream creator function that receives the stream callbacks and returns a\n  // GrpcStream object.
